## 2026-06-18 — Repair: parse the REAL nested-`data` event shape (FRD-06) + drop the fabricated void-secret date (FRD-10), baseline green
**What:** The build engine's `verify.sh` was red on 4 failures across two FRD-gate reviewer anchors. (1) **FRD-06 — real event shape.** `src/app/projects/[slug]/_party/_tests/frd-06-realdata.reviewer.test.ts` (3 fails) proved that the WO-06-012 implementer built `lib/events.ts` against a *flat* fixture where the enriched fields (`role`, `wo`, `frd`, `phase`, `activity`, `mode`) sit at the top level — but the REAL plugin emitter (`plugin/templates/shared/.claude/workflows/pandacorp-build.js` line 51, confirmed against `~/.claude/dashboard-events.ndjson`) nests them under a `data` object: `{"event":"AgentWorking","at":…,"project":…,"data":{"role":…,"wo":…,"frd":…,"phase":…,"activity":…,"mode":…}}`. Against the real stream the parser read `undefined` for every enriched field, so La Fragua never activated (`snap.active=false`, no running WOs, default mode). Fixed `applyEnrichedFields` to prefer a nested `data` object (falling back to top-level for the flat/legacy shape — backward-compat AC-06-008.2) and mapped the emitter's `wo` field to `workOrder` (the old `work_order`→`workOrder` mapping kept, taking precedence). (2) **FRD-10 — honest secret unlock.** `src/app/achievements/_tests/frd-10-integration.reviewer.test.tsx` (1 fail) confirmed the reviewer's reopen of WO-10-001: the `void-side` secret in `predicates.ts` returned a fabricated unlock date `"2026-01-01"`; `IdeaCard` has no date field, so no source can prove it (violates AC-10-004.3 + blueprint §5 honesty contract). Applied the reviewer's recommended option (b): the `check` now omits the date (return type relaxed to `{ date?: string; project: string }`), unlocking with only the provable `project`. Corrected the matching decorative implementer test (AC-10-004.2) that codified the fabricated date — it now asserts `voidSecret.date` is `undefined`.
**Why:** Baseline repair (the build engine's `verify.sh` was red on two FRD-gate reviewer anchors, both genuine production defects: a parser that doesn't match the real emitter, and a fabricated date). Not an owner decision: both reviewers authored the RED anchors and the exact fixes this matches (FRD-10's recorded as "Concrete fix (next run)"); no AC weakened — the only test edit corrected a vacuous assertion that encoded the bug.
**Verified:** `bash .pandacorp/verify.sh` green — 238 test files, 5957 pass (2 expected-fail, 5 skipped); biome + tsc clean. Both reviewer anchors now GREEN; the WO-06-012 flat-shape tests, events unit/adversarial suites, and the achievements engine suite all still pass (no regression).
**Impact:** `src/lib/events/events.ts` (nested-`data` enriched-field parsing + `wo`→`workOrder` mapping); `src/lib/achievements/predicates.ts` (void-side: no fabricated date, optional `date` in `SecretDefinition.check`); `src/lib/achievements/_tests/achievements.test.ts` (corrected the decorative date assertion); WO-10-001 frontmatter → IN_REVIEW + resolution Status Note (back to the FRD-10 gate for re-verification; never VERIFIED by the implementer — DR-015/DR-050). ## 2026-06-18 — Repair: un-nest the recovery CopyButton from the row navigation Link (WO-03-004, FRD-03 gate green)
**What:** The FRD-03 close-out `verify.sh` was red on the reviewer anchor `src/app/portfolio/_tests/frd-03-nested-interactive.reviewer.test.tsx` (1/1 fail) — the reviewer had reopened WO-03-004 because the prior integration repair (which correctly composed `BusinessSnapshot` + `RecoveryHint` into the live rail) placed `RecoveryHint` — and therefore its `CopyButton` (`<button>`) — INSIDE the row's navigation `<Link>` (an `<a>`). A `<button>` nested in an `<a>` is invalid interactive-content nesting (HTML spec / WCAG 4.1.2): React flags it as a hydration-class defect and a click on "copiar" also fired the row's `?project=` navigation, hijacking the copyable recovery the FRD requires (AC-03-006.3). Restructured `SelectableProjectRail.tsx` per the reviewer's option 1: the `<article>` is now the row container (owns the block-level chrome, `data-selected`, `aria-label`), and the `<Link>` wraps ONLY the navigational header (name + stage + indicator). `StatusChips`, `BusinessSnapshot` and `RecoveryHint` are now siblings of the link inside the `<article>`, so no `<button>` descends from the `<a>`. The link gets a small negative margin to keep its hit-target spanning the row's horizontal padding; `aria-current="page"` stays on the selected row's link.
**Why:** Baseline repair (the build engine's `verify.sh` was red on a defect in FRD-03's WO-03-004, landed in the same commit as FRD-17's wiring but owned by FRD-03's gate). Not an owner decision: the reviewer authored the RED anchor and the concrete fix (file:line) this matches; the change is DOM-nesting only, no AC altered, no test weakened.
**Verified:** `bash .pandacorp/verify.sh` green — 221 test files, 5625 pass (2 expected-fail, 5 skipped); biome + tsc clean. Also green scoped `--since dbcf75d`. The nested-interactive reviewer anchor is now GREEN; the snapshot/badge/recovery integration anchors (`frd-03-integration.reviewer.test.tsx`, `frd-03-integration.gate.reviewer.test.tsx`) and the `wo-03-004.test.tsx` rail/link/data-selected suite all still pass (no regression).
**Impact:** `src/app/portfolio/SelectableProjectRail.tsx` (un-nest the row composition); the reviewer anchor `src/app/portfolio/_tests/frd-03-nested-interactive.reviewer.test.tsx` committed with the green state; WO-03-004 frontmatter → IN_REVIEW + repair Status Note (back to the FRD-03 gate for re-verification; never VERIFIED by the implementer — DR-015/DR-050). FRD-17's seven work orders left untouched (all correct/IN_REVIEW; this was never an FRD-17 defect).

Repointed both to `var(--color-tier-5, var(--color-agent-product-manager))` (a surviving canonical agent token, golden `oklch(0.7 0.18 85)`, distinct from the tier-1..4 fallbacks). The companion FRD-06 engine split (`engine.ts` 605→414 + `engine/types.ts` + `engine/slots.ts`, behavior-preserving) — already done and verified but held uncommitted by the FRD-06 pass pending this regression — is committed alongside, since a coherent green HEAD depends on it (the 605-line engine otherwise breaks the max-lines guard).
**Why:** Not an owner decision: WO-10-006 already mandates "tier color tokens fall back to existing agent tokens until FRD-13 defines them explicitly", and the FRD-13 reviewer explicitly authorized repointing the fallback to a surviving token. The fix is behavior-preserving — the broken fallback previously resolved to no color at all. Resetting the stale BLOCKED/needs-owner state (WO-06-004) and PLANNED state (WO-13-002) to IN_REVIEW because their sole blocker is now resolved; cleared the `blocked` entry in `status.yaml`.
**Verified:** `bash .pandacorp/verify.sh` green (187 files, 5145 pass + 2 expected-fail + 5 skipped; biome + tsc + madge + structure/max-lines guards clean). The reviewer probe is now 2/2 green; all 131 FRD-10 achievements tests still pass.
**Impact:** `src/app/achievements/StatsPanel.tsx`, `src/app/achievements/ChainCard/ChainCard.tsx`, FRD-06 engine split (3 files), `.pandacorp/status.yaml` (cleared `blocked`), WO-06-004 + WO-13-002 frontmatter → IN_REVIEW, `.pandacorp/inbox/decisions.md` (blocker closed).

## 2026-06-18 — Fix: removed stray `"use server"` from manual + configuration pages (`next build` clean)
**What:** Deleted the erroneous top-level `"use server";` from `src/app/manual/page.tsx` and `src/app/configuration/page.tsx`. They are **Server Components** (the default — no directive); `"use server"` had marked them as Server-Actions modules, which require every export to be an async function, so the build rejected the page component and the `metadata` const. Both files only export `metadata` + a sync page → the directive was pure mistake.
**Why:** `next build` failed with "Server Actions must be async functions" (surfaced during the `src/` migration; the directive predated it). `next dev` — how MC runs — tolerated it, so it had stayed latent. Also a `nextjs.md` rule violation (Server Components by default; `"use server"` is for actions).
**Verified:** `next build` now completes clean (full route table, exit 0); full test suite green (4919 passed). No regression test added on purpose — it would be a loose `*.test.tsx` (violating the `_tests/` rule mid-migration); the real guard is `next build` in CI, to be wired with the compliance migration.
**Impact:** `src/app/manual/page.tsx`, `src/app/configuration/page.tsx`.

## 2026-06-18 — Party redesign: two faithful views (La Fragua + La Campaña), placement decided
**What:** Designed (in `prototype/`) a redesign of the Party so it reflects how the engine **actually** builds, replacing the fictitious cast (researcher/backend/frontend/testing wandering 4 zones, chatting, handing off live) that FRD-06 currently ships. Two views: **La Fragua** — the *build* as a living world (1 sprite = 1 running `implementer` work order; wave = mode; the `reviewer` gate is one-per-FRD; the parchment = the real `Status Note` doc hand-off; deep mode = a sequential `test-writer → backend-dev →📄contrato→ frontend-dev` relay; the scene is always the FRD-in-build so it scales to 100+ WO projects); **La Campaña** — the full 6-phase pipeline with the real specialist team per phase, communicating by documents across time. **Placement decided:** La Fragua → **Portfolio → project → Party tab (FRD-06)**; La Campaña → **the board card detail (FRD-02)** as its first of three horizontal tabs (Campaña · Documentos · Comandos), because the board is where an idea lives across its *whole* lifecycle, not just the build. A third role-color touch-point lands in **FRD-13**. Navigable mockups: `prototype/party-proposal.html`, `prototype/party-pipeline.html`, embedded in place in `prototype/index.html` (auto-sizing iframes, no inner scroll). Full design spec: **`prototype/party-redesign-spec.md`**.
**Why:** FRD-06 misrepresented the engine — a generalist `implementer` per work order orchestrated by a deterministic script with document hand-offs (DR-013), NOT a team of specialists chatting live; the specialists live in *other phases*. The owner chose to fix the model before cementing the agent views. Faithfulness first, then the RPG magic. The owner validated the direction across the prototype iterations.
**Impact:** Design only (in `prototype/`), nothing in `app/` yet. To production via **`/pandacorp:iterate`** (rewrite **FRD-06**, extend **FRD-02**, touch **FRD-13**). Prerequisite already landed: the build engine now emits **enriched Party telemetry** (frd/phase/activity/mode) so the views run on real data — plugin **v8.11.0** (`plugin/docs/decision-log.md`), spec §7. The mode selector + pause/reset in the mockup are **demo-only** (MC is read-only; production reads the mode from state).

The work orders themselves were not touched.
**Why:** Surfaced while clarifying FRD-06's real state (it is **built and `IN_REVIEW`, awaiting the gate** — neither "verified" nor "not started"). Per the new source-of-truth rule (build-orchestration §1 / DR-050), an FRD's status is derived from its work orders.

The load-bearing integration risk — that the board column (`deriveColumn`) and the card-detail command (`nextStep`) read the same two axes (card status + project phase) and must never disagree about the lifecycle stage — was exercised end-to-end, including the B1'/I3 undefined-phase anchors (both paths fall back coherently: board → `documented`, detail → `/pandacorp:spec`, never a misleading stage). The single-write invariant (AC-02-007.1) was verified against the **real** `discardIdea` over a temp filesystem (not the mocked unit test): only the target card is rewritten, siblings byte-for-byte intact, body + all other frontmatter preserved verbatim, `revalidatePath` fires only on success, path traversal (`../secret`) rejected end-to-end writing nothing.
**Impact:** `docs/frds/frd-02-ideas-board/` (six WO frontmatter + frd.md + blueprint.md → VERIFIED), two reviewer test files added (`app/board/frd-02.integration.reviewer.test.tsx`, `app/board/discard-write.integration.reviewer.test.ts`, +24 tests), `.pandacorp/status.yaml` (`work_orders_done` 27, `last_green_sha`), `.pandacorp/comms/progress.md`. **Adversarial round (DR-015) + mutation check (DR-016):** 3 mutants injected and killed — CMD_RELEASE→design broke 3 coherence tests; `deriveColumn` release→shipped broke 2; `actions.ts` revalidate-without-success-guard broke 3 no-churn tests. Tests not decorative. Zero production-code drift (only reviewer test files added). Non-blocking finding carried from WO-02-002: Spanish UI strings hardcoded (no project-wide i18n layer yet) — deferred to a dedicated i18n WO.

## 2026-06-16 — WO-11-001 fix: deep-freeze BUILD_MODES catalog entries (B1 blocker from reviewer)
**What:** Fixed the shallow-freeze defect in `lib/constants.ts` (B1 from `docs/reviews/wo-11-001-review.md`). The original `Object.freeze([…])` was shallow — the array itself was frozen but each entry object remained mutable, allowing `BUILD_MODES[0].id = "x"` to silently corrupt the catalog singleton for all consumers. Applied a deep-freeze: each entry is now wrapped with `Object.freeze(m)` inside a `.map()` before the outer `Object.freeze`. Added the reviewer-authored adversarial test suite `lib/build-modes.adversarial.test.ts` (20 tests, covering case/whitespace-variant modes, coercion-literal poison, JSON-object values, substring rejection, prototype-pollution keys, slug-with-`:` isolation, unicode slugs, and write-path throw-safety for `rememberMode`). All 61 WO-11-001 tests green; verify.sh (biome + tsc + vitest) passes.
**Why:** The reviewer (DR-015 different-model-family review) correctly identified that the immutability guarantee documented in the code comment was false at runtime. A mutation anywhere in the app would permanently corrupt the catalog singleton, breaking `getRememberedMode`'s `VALID_MODES` set and causing every validation check to pass unknown strings. Deep-freezing each entry is the correct fix: it causes `BUILD_MODES[0].id = "x"` to throw in strict mode (ESM files are always strict), making the corruption attempt visible and loud rather than silent.
**Impact:** Modified `mission-control/lib/constants.ts` (deep-freeze entries); added `mission-control/lib/build-modes.adversarial.test.ts`; `docs/api.md` updated (`BUILD_MODES is frozen` note now accurately says "deep-frozen").

## 2026-06-16 — WO-13-001: token schema validator + agent-color/state-vocab key maps (IF-13-tokens, IF-13-agent-colors, IF-13-state-vocab)
**What:** Implemented the pure TypeScript module `app/_design/tokens.ts` (WO-13-001). Exports: `validateTokenSchema` (validates `design-tokens.json` shape against blueprint §3 contract — OKLCH keys, three theme variants including highContrast, all 10 agent roles, exactly 3 elevation levels, spacing scale, motion durations all <300ms, 2–3 easing tokens); `AGENT_ROLES` / `AgentRole` / `AGENT_COLOR` (canonical role→CSS-token-key map, single source for FRD-06 and FRD-12 DAG); `AGENT_STATES` / `AgentState` / `STATE_BADGE` (icon+Spanish-label per state, 6 states — working/idle/failed/completed/blocked/reviewing). All 39 tests green; verify.sh (biome + tsc + vitest) passes. Published the internal module contract in `docs/api.md`.
**Why:** WO-13-001 establishes the typed contract that downstream UI WOs (FRD-06 Party, FRD-12 DAG, CMP-13-state-badge) depend on. Without it, every feature would define its own role/state vocabulary, creating duplication and drift. The `[key: string]: unknown` index signatures on `OklchTokens`, `ThemeTokens`, and `TokenSchema` are intentional — they allow the test file's `as Record<string, unknown>` cast pattern used for mutation testing (structuredClone + delete key). The `pick()` helper avoids biome's `useLiteralKeys` rule for dynamic key access on unknown records.
**Impact:** New `mission-control/app/_design/tokens.ts`, `mission-control/docs/api.md`; safe biome fixes applied to `app/_design/tokens.test.ts` and `components/CopyButton.test.tsx` (import ordering + format, no behavior change).

## 2026-06-16 — Pandacorp overlay materialized (6.0.0 → 7.0.0): Mission Control becomes a buildable factory project
**What:** Mission Control was documented by hand inside the factory and never went through `/pandacorp:scaffold`, so it carried product docs + a hand-written `.pandacorp/status.yaml` but **none of the overlay machinery**. Materialized the full integration overlay from the v7 templates so `/pandacorp:blueprint` → `/pandacorp:implement` can run on it: created `CLAUDE.md` + `AGENTS.md` (thin imports + durable conventions), `.pandacorp/guide.md` + `.pandacorp/README.md` (managed layer), `.claude/workflows/pandacorp-build.js` (the build engine — the previously missing blocker for `/implement`), `.claude/settings.json` (deny `rm -rf` / force-push / `.env` reads), a project-level `.gitignore` (adds `node_modules/.next/coverage/.env` on top of the root's MC ignores), and the gitignored `.pandacorp/comms/iteration.md`. Bumped `overlay_version` 6.0.0 → 7.0.0 (`created_with` stays 6.0.0). The DR-049 feature-centric migration (upgrade step 2b) did NOT run — MC was already on that layout.
**Why:** The owner decided to build Mission Control with Pandacorp itself (dogfooding) instead of building it separately. An audit found MC's overlay was *declared* (status said 6.0.0) but never *materialized*; in particular the build engine `pandacorp-build.js` was absent, which would block `/implement`. This is the equivalent of a manual `/pandacorp:upgrade` for a never-scaffolded, in-factory project. MC is the special case of a project living INSIDE the factory repo, so its new `CLAUDE.md` records the deviations: no own git / never `git init`; factory root is one level up (`process.cwd()/..`, override `PANDACORP_FACTORY_ROOT`); `return_type` personal so the economic arc is skipped; `/release` = run locally on `127.0.0.1` (no deploy, no production gate).
**Impact:** New `mission-control/{CLAUDE.md, AGENTS.md, .gitignore}`, `mission-control/.claude/{settings.json, workflows/pandacorp-build.js}`, `mission-control/.pandacorp/{guide.md, README.md}`; `mission-control/.pandacorp/status.yaml` `overlay_version` → 7.0.0. Pending before build: decide the v1 FRD scope (18 FRDs is too many for one blueprint), reconcile `PLAN.md` (its `git init` step doesn't apply in-repo; its state table predates the unified model), then `/pandacorp:blueprint`. Plugin-side follow-ups identified, not yet done: add the DR-045/048 preflight to the `blueprint` skill (it lacks the auto-upgrade that `implement`/`iterate`/`bug` have), and namespace `emit-event.sh` events by project so the Party panel can tell builds apart.

## 2026-06-16 — FRD-18: Dashboard ("Inicio") as the landing command center
**What:** New **FRD-18**. Mission Control gains a **Dashboard** as its default landing view (the old behavior opened straight into a tab); the five tabs (Board/Portfolio/Achievements/Configuration/Manual) stay reachable from the nav. The dashboard is a read-only command center with five zones, top to bottom: (1) **Desde tu última visita** — a digest of *events* (work orders closed/failed, phase moves, decisions queued, lessons captured), not totals; (2) **Tu turno** — a queue of ONLY human-gate items (pending decisions, shipped-awaiting-`review-launch`, memory backlog nudge, ideas to prioritize) — `advance_pending` deliberately excluded (it lives on the Board); (3) **Pulso de la fábrica** — a small funnel + the one metric that matters (idea→shipped conversion) + the live/no-signal indicator; (4) **Construcción y cartera** — per-project cards enriched with age-in-stage, *en vivo*/*sin señal*, inline blocker reason, and shipped shown as *estable · en operación*; (5) **Tu progreso** — the honest gamification strip (FRD-09). It composes FRD-09/12/13 and surfaces the FRD-01/15/16/17 banners. Built and approved iteratively in the prototype (`view: dashboard`): a first pass, then a research-informed v2 (added the digest, enriched the cartera, reframed the pulse as a funnel, dropped `advance_pending` from the queue per owner feedback).
**Why:** The owner asked for a landing screen that helps him *decide and take the next step* — "what needs me, where do I go" — with real value, not vanity metrics, plus a touch of honest gamification. We grounded the design in web research on analogous products (Devin Desktop's agent board, Linear Inbox, PagerDuty's "your open incidents", Vercel/GitHub-Actions build status, AgentCenter, Datadog's "alert on a lack of data", Kanban aging-WIP, HITL review-queue UX, NN/g action-centric dashboards, Lean Analytics OMTM, Octalysis White-Hat). The convergent principles: lead with a human-gate queue, manufacture substance from *events* (the since-last-visit digest) not counters, show age/stuck and no-signal not just status, tie every number to a decision, stay quiet when healthy, and reward outcomes only.
**The "Desde tu última visita" marker (key design call):** the owner flagged that with an always-open app, defining "last visit" as "last page load" would reset on every refresh and show nothing. Resolved: the `visto_hasta` marker is **persisted client-local state** (survives refresh and tab close) and advances ONLY on acknowledgement ("marcar visto") or on acting on an item — a refresh never moves it, so unseen events are never lost (email-style read/unread). When caught up, the section is never empty: it falls back to a dimmed last-24h rolling window, and (always-open) should tick up live as events arrive.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-18-dashboard.md` (new); `frd-01-data-reading.md` (reads the event stream for the digest + persists the local `visto_hasta` marker, clarified as UI state not a factory/project write); `docs/prd.md` (Scope v1 + product goal 0 + FRD range → FRD-18); `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (new `dashboard` view + default landing, `digestSection()` with localStorage-backed seen marker, enriched portfolio cards, funnel pulse, `goproj`/`goidea`/`goboard`/`seen`/`seen-sim`/`seen-reset` handlers). Verified live in the preview: all zones render, navigation works, the seen-marker survives refresh, zero console errors. Spec-anchored mock data in the prototype; the Next.js app will read real events/state. Approved as a **first version** ("not 100% convinced, ship and iterate"). No Manual change needed — the dashboard is MC's own surface, not a new factory operable item (skills/agents/rules/standards), so DR-046's derived Reference is untouched.

Hand-authored Concept page per DR-046's Guides/Concepts discipline (the Reference catalogs still auto-derive separately).

The button stays always visible; clicking it opens a modal with dark backdrop + blur showing the four intake options (`explore`, `new-idea`, `discover`, `recommend`) as icon cards with description and copy-command row. Clicking the backdrop or ✕ closes it. Also corrected FRD-02: it was missing `/pandacorp:explore` from the intake command list.

## 2026-06-15 — FRD-03: missing-path badge + recovery command in Portfolio panel
**What:** Added acceptance criteria to **FRD-03** for the case where a project registered in the portfolio no longer exists on disk (folder deleted or moved): the Portfolio panel SHALL show a `⚠️ path not found` badge on that project row, plus a copyable recovery command (`git clone <repo> <path>` + re-run sync-portfolio) if a `repo:` URL exists, or a plain warning if there is no remote. Same read-only + copyable-command pattern as FRD-15/16 banners. Badge disappears once the path is back on disk.
**Why:** The owner asked what happens when a project folder is deleted locally — the factory still tracks it but the user has no path forward. The plugin side (sync-portfolio step 4) now gives recovery instructions; the FRD side documents what the Next.js app must show when it reads the portfolio.

Spec-only for MC — the prototype doesn't simulate it; the Next.js app will implement it when the Portfolio panel is built.

## 2026-06-15 — FRD-17: Proposals inbox (self-learning gate + self-suggestion)
**What:** New **FRD-17**. Mission Control gains a **Proposals inbox** ("Propuestas / Crónica del gremio") — the owner-facing surface of the self-learning loop (DR-047) and the place where MC suggests improvements on its own. It aggregates four streams: candidate lessons from `factory/memory/`, promotion proposals (a recurring lesson → standard/rule/skill), prune proposals from `/pandacorp:memory review`, and **self-suggestions** MC computes locally (bottlenecks, velocity alerts, unused skill/agent, decision-rule friction, a lesson recurring across ≥2 projects, a shipped project that merits `/pandacorp:review-launch`). For each, it shows the evidence + the exact command to act — and never acts itself (read-only, like FRD-15/16). Extends FRD-14's chips with a proposals stream; honest/dismissible per FRD-09. Also a **memory-health panel** (owner's request): pending raw-note count, candidate-lesson count, and `/pandacorp:memory` last-run staleness, with a nudge command when there's a backlog — it doubles as the on-demand refine trigger, so the cadence is scheduled sweep + this reminder (NOT tied to `implement`). And a durable **promotions queue** (lessons carry a `promotion: proposed/approved/rejected` field set by `/memory review` + `learn`): the owner reviews the full list of rules-to-promote and decides whenever — via `/pandacorp:memory status` today and this page when the app is built (owner's request).
**Why:** The owner asked for two things on Mission Control: a place to approve the lessons/promotions the factory learns, and for the app to "auto-suggest" improvements the more it is used, without being asked — the human gate of DR-047 and the visible face of the loop (`docs/proposals/09-self-learning-factory.md`). Computing suggestions locally from data MC already reads (events, status, portfolio, `factory/memory/`) keeps it read-only and Claude-call-free (FRD-01).
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-17-proposals-inbox.md` (new). Spec-only — Mission Control isn't built yet (the prototype will simulate it). Factory side: the loop's engine shipped in plugin v6.1.0 (`librarian` agent + `/pandacorp:memory`), DR-047. Pending: reconcile the prototype Manual catalogs (the new `memory` skill, `librarian` agent, DR-047/DR-048) and add a "Self-learning loop" Concept page (DR-046, FRD-08).

## 2026-06-15 — Read the new .pandacorp/ project layer; MC dogfoods it (DR-048)
**What:** Project state moved from `docs/status.yaml` to `.pandacorp/status.yaml` (DR-048), so the data-reading FRDs were updated: FRD-01/02/04/14/16 now read `.pandacorp/status.yaml` and the `.pandacorp/inbox/` (bugs, decisions) + `.pandacorp/comms/` layers. Mission Control **dogfoods** the new structure: its own `docs/{status.yaml,idea-origin.md,summary.md}` moved to `mission-control/.pandacorp/`.
**Why:** Consistency with the factory's new project structure (see `factory/decision-log.md`, same date, DR-048). MC reads every project's state; that path changed.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/{frd-01,frd-02,frd-04,frd-14,frd-16}.md` (paths), `mission-control/.pandacorp/{status.yaml,idea-origin.md,comms/summary.md}` (moved), root `.gitignore` (MC comms paths). The HTML prototype's mock paths are cosmetic; reconcile when the Next.js app reads real files.

## 2026-06-15 — Manual (FRD-08) reflects the factory: derived Reference + reconciled prototype (DR-046)
**What:** FRD-08 now requires the Manual's **Reference** catalogs (commands, agents, decision rules, standards) to be **derived from the canonical source** at build/read time — the plugin skill+agent frontmatter under `plugin/skills/` & `plugin/agents/`, `factory/decisions/registry.yaml`, `factory/standards/` — not a hand-maintained copy, plus a criterion that the Manual stays in sync (Reference auto-derived; Guides/Concepts by the documentation discipline). Reconciled the HTML prototype's catalogs against today's factory: added skills `review-launch` + `adopt`, agent `implementer`, rules DR-040..DR-046, and the `documentation` standard — closing a drift of 2 skills / 1 agent / 6 rules / 1 standard. Catalog now: 20 skills (7 fábrica + 13 proyecto), 13 agents, 46 rules (last DR-046), 14 standards.
**Why:** Owner's rule (DR-046, see [factory/decision-log.md](../../factory/decision-log.md) same date): every relevant factory-workflow change must surface in the Manual, and the future Next.js app must build the Reference from the real artifacts so it can't drift. The prototype had fallen behind — exactly the failure the rule prevents.
**Context:** Mechanism chosen by the owner = derive the Reference (drift-proof) + discipline for the hand-authored prose. The prototype's `CONFIG.{skills,agents,rules,estandares}` arrays remain the hand-reconciled stand-in until the Next.js app derives the catalogs from source (FRD-08 prototype note).
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-08-documentation.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (`CONFIG` arrays). Factory-side: `factory/decisions/registry.yaml` (DR-046) + root `CLAUDE.md` ("Decision log" section) — twin entry in `factory/decision-log.md` (same date). Verified in preview: Referencia → Comandos renders the reconciled catalog (the new `/review-launch` and `/adopt` cards appear; counts 7+13), no console errors; CONFIG counts confirmed by evaluation (20/13/46/14).

## 2026-06-15 — FRD-16: orphan-project detection (adopt? banner)
**What:** New FRD-16. Mission Control scans the projects folder (`projects_path` from the profile, else the factory's parent) for git repos that are NOT in the portfolio and have NO Pandacorp marker, and surfaces them as a dismissible "Unregistered project — adopt?" banner pointing to `/pandacorp:adopt`. A folder WITH the marker but missing from the portfolio suggests `/pandacorp:sync-portfolio` instead. Read-only and bounded to the projects folder's immediate children; sibling of FRD-15 (plugin drift): detect a gap, show the command, don't act.
**Why:** The new brownfield path (DR-045, `/pandacorp:adopt`) needs a way to be discovered — otherwise an external project the owner built stays invisible to the factory. This closes the loop so Mission Control nudges adoption, mirroring how FRD-15 nudges the plugin update.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-16-orphan-project-detection.md` (new). Factory side: `factory/decisions/registry.yaml` (DR-045), `factory/decision-log.md` (same date). Spec-only — Mission Control isn't built yet (the prototype simulates it with an `ORPHANS` flag).

## 2026-06-15 — Board column derivation (phase bridge), portfolio business columns, drift-banner fix
**What:** FRD-02 now **derives** a card's column from two axes (card status pre-project; the project's `phase` for `in-pipeline` cards) instead of grouping by `status` alone — fixing the design/architecture/building columns that no card status ever produced (mapping: product→Documentada, design→Diseño, architecture→Arquitectura, implementation/release→building, operation→shipped; missing project → falls back to Documentada). FRD-01 reads the project phase as the column source for in-pipeline cards and also reads `pending_bugs`/`last_green_sha`/`safe_to_test`. FRD-03 shows each shipped project's business snapshot (users/return/verdict from `/pandacorp:review-launch`, DR-043). FRD-15's drift banner now compares `gitCommitSha` (not the semver `version`, which never matched). Mission Control's own `status.yaml` got the 5 missing template fields.
**Why:** The re-audit found the board couldn't place mid-pipeline cards from the frontmatter alone (the card freezes at `in-pipeline`), and the drift banner read the wrong field so it couldn't warn when the installed plugin fell behind.
**Context:** The prototype (mock data) still groups by a `status` that crams the column value in; the real Next.js app implements the FRD-02 derivation — not worth rewriting the 2.4 MB mock now.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/{frd-01,frd-02,frd-03,frd-15}.md`, `mission-control/docs/status.yaml`. Factory-side state model: `factory/decision-log.md` and `factory/ideas/decision-log.md` (same date).

## 2026-06-15 — Mission Control's UI is in Spanish (made explicit)
**What:** Stated explicitly, in the PRD and the factory's Language convention, that Mission Control's entire user-facing UI (copy, labels, `aria-label`s) is in **Spanish** — it's the owner's tool, operated in Spanish. The underlying code/identifiers stay English; only the UI copy is Spanish. This is the committed exception to "committed = English".
**Why:** The owner asked to state it clearly, beyond the existing note in the design brief.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/prd.md` (User), `factory/standards/conventions.md` (Language). Already reflected in `design/brief.md` and the prototype.

## 2026-06-15 — Prototype + status.yaml aligned to the English language policy
**What:** Migrated the prototype's machine identifiers to English while keeping the Spanish UI: pipeline enums (`PIPE`/`LBL` keys → discovered/documented/design/architecture/building/shipped, labels stay Spanish), idea `status`/`return_type` mock data and filters, the build-mode tokens (balanced/powerful/deep) with Spanish display labels, and the zone keys (research/review/analytics/security) to match the renamed assets. `docs/status.yaml` now holds machine state only (English); the Spanish narrative moved to the gitignored `docs/summary.md`. All docs (PRD, FRDs, PLAN, PARTY, design briefs) translated to English; the prototype UI copy stays Spanish.
**Why:** Part of the repo-wide language migration (see `factory/decision-log.md`, same date).
**Impact:** `mission-control/prototype/index.html`, `mission-control/docs/**`, `embed-images.py`/`crop-avatars.py`. Verified in preview: board renders with Spanish column labels, no console errors, no raw enums.

## 2026-06-15 — Configuration reflects external-services + DR-032..039
**What:** The prototype (Configuration → Standards and Rules) was synced with the factory: the **external-services** standard card (Operation domain) was added to the "Craft Codex", and the decision registry — which cut off at DR-031 — now includes **DR-032..039** (iterate without advancing, personal data, plugin versioning, Vercel/payments, external services + accounts, secrets/provisioning, push at gates, recommendations based on the profile). The stack summary now names the services (R2, Resend, Kit, Sentry, PostHog, Polar).
**Why:** Configuration is the source of context for understanding the factory; it had to reflect the new standard and decisions, not fall out of date.
**Impact:** `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (the `CONFIG.estandares` and `decisiones` arrays + stack summary).

## 2026-06-15 — Title "Pandacorp Mission Control" + Guild vs Party codified
**What:** (1) The app's visible title becomes **"Pandacorp Mission Control"** (topbar + `<title>`): Pandacorp (brand) + Mission Control (the app). (2) It was clarified that **Guild (gremio)** and **Party** are two **distinct** RPG layers — not synonyms — and the boundary was **codified** in [FRD-09](frds/frd-09-gamification/frd.md): guild = the operator/factory meta layer (level/XP, guild Hall/Codex/Commands); party = the agents of one concrete project (RPG panel, FRD-06). The phrases where they were mixed were cleaned up ("The party works in the guild…" → "…in its room…"; PARTY.md "by a guild" → "by the guild's room").
**Why:** The owner noticed "guild" in several places and wondered if it was the same as Party. It isn't (a guild has many parties); both layers are intentional. Writing down the boundary avoids confusing them in the future.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-09-gamification.md` (new "Vocabulary: Guild vs Party" section), `mission-control/PARTY.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html` (title + feed).

## 2026-06-15 — Rename: the app is "Mission Control"; the RPG panel is "Party"
**What:** We reassigned the names. The **whole app** (formerly "cockpit") is now called **Mission Control** — the center from which the entire factory is controlled. The **per-project RPG panel** (formerly "Mission Control") becomes **Party**: the subtab where you see your party of agents working live. "Pandacorp" remains the factory/brand. The `cockpit/` → `mission-control/` folder was renamed, the panel's canonical docs (`MISSION-CONTROL.md` → `PARTY.md`, `frd-06-mission-control.md` → `frd-06-party.md`), the prototype (topbar, `<title>`, "Party" subtab, manual texts) and `.claude/launch.json`. Verified in preview: "Mission Control" topbar, "Party" subtab, RPG map and KPIs intact, no console errors.
**Why:** By convention (NASA, macOS), "Mission Control" names the center that supervises and commands the ENTIRE operation, not a sub-panel; having it on the little panel inverted the meaning and was sometimes used as a synonym for the app. The analogy now is clean: Pandacorp (organization) → Mission Control (its control center = the app) → Party (the crew of agents on each mission, in line with the "party" language the prototype already used).
**Impact:** the `mission-control/` folder (formerly `cockpit/`), `mission-control/PARTY.md`, `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-06-party.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html`, `.claude/launch.json`. Repo-wide change (CLAUDE.md, README, plugin/skills, standards, registry.yaml, hook): see the twin entry in [factory/decision-log.md](../../factory/decision-log.md).

## 2026-06-15 — Onboarding gate + board tags (category + return)
**What:** Mission Control gains an **onboarding gate**: if it doesn't find `factory/profile.md`, it shows — before anything else — a banner asking to run `/pandacorp:onboarding` (FRD-01). On the board, each card goes from a single tag (monetizable/personal/both) to **two**: **category** (solution type: web/mobile/desktop/AI/claude-code/prompts/automation/CLI/rework) with an icon, and **return** (monetary/opportunity/personal/mixed) with color; the filter is now by category (FRD-02). HTML prototype updated and verified in preview.
**Why:** Without a profile the factory can't make aligned recommendations (hence the gate). A single binary tag captured neither the project type nor the return model (money or opportunity); two orthogonal axes make it clear on the board.
**Impact:** `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-01-data-reading.md`, `mission-control/docs/frds/frd-02-ideas-board.md`, `mission-control/prototype/index.html`. Related: `factory/ideas/_idea-template.md`, DR-039.

## 2026-06-14 — Mission Control decision log created
**What:** The Mission Control decision log starts.
**Why:** Part of the factory's "document everything" discipline — see [factory/decision-log.md](../../factory/decision-log.md).
